Since Russian troops invaded Ukraine in late February, Delfast\u2019s top priority has been to see its Ukrainian team of 30 safely evacuated from the most dangerous parts of the country.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n When not focusing on sales, marketing, R&D and customer support, Delfast\u2019s smaller team of seven employees based in Los Angeles has been pleading with U.S. politicians and the European Commission to supply Ukraine with anti-aircraft missiles and fighter jets that could help Ukraine gain back some control over its air space, and, hopefully, put a stop to this war.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Delfast\u2019s co-founders, Daniel Tonkopi and Serhiy Denysenko, say they have always believed in safeguarding the future. When they founded Delfast in 2014, originally as a delivery company, Tonkoply and Denysenko knew that providing couriers with green transportation options would be critical to the company\u2019s operations.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n \t \n\t\t \n\t\t\tThe most important thing for an entrepreneur, and in general for any leader, is to protect the team and be completely honest with them during a tough time.\t\t\t\t\t\t\tDaniel Tonkopi, co-founder of Delfast<\/cite>\n\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/span><\/p>\n The founders soon realized that a bike with the power, range and battery life their couriers needed didn\u2019t exist, and so they set out to build one. In 2017, backed by a Kickstarter campaign that saw the company raise $165,000, the startup began manufacturing a bike to fit its needs \u2013 one that promptly <\/span>won the Guinness Book of World Records<\/span><\/a> for the greatest distance traveled on an electric motorbike on a single charge.<\/span><\/p>\n More recently, the Delfast Top 3.0 e-motorbike <\/span>won Forbes\u2019 fastest e-bike of the year<\/span><\/a> in 2022 after the company announced some serious <\/span>upgrades to the vehicle during CES<\/span><\/a>.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n We spoke with Delfast\u2019s co-founders to discuss what it\u2019s like running a startup during a war, how the startup is considering breaking into new business verticals, and the importance of always having a Plan B.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n The following interview, part of an ongoing series with founders who are building transportation companies, has been edited for length and clarity.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n Note: Serhiy Denysenko\u2019s answers were translated from Ukrainian by a member of Delfast\u2019s team for TechCrunch.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n TC: Serhiy, you’re on the ground in Kyiv. What’s your day-to-day like?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. It\u2019s important to keep in touch and know that everyone is fine, or as fine as is possible right now.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Besides my work as a COO, I\u2019ve been helping with volunteering, getting supplies and medicine to people, and this is something that pretty much every Ukrainian is now doing. I had my family relocated to Hungary, so I feel more or less safe, and I\u2019m just trying to work as much as possible and do my best in every possible area, whether that\u2019s supporting the company or supporting Ukraine in general.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n How are you managing your team through this crisis? What\u2019s changed?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>We got used to working remotely during Coronavirus times, so we have our task tracker, where everyone can see his or her task. Every Monday, we have an online Zoom meeting. Previously we only had these meetings at the executive level, but now during the war, we are gathering all together, just to see each other\u2019s faces and ask how they\u2019re doing, how\u2019s everyone feeling. Just to talk with everybody.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n <\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":" “Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. the robo-berry"},"content":{"rendered":" If you’ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that’s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren’t super good at because they tend to be… crushy. But this robo-berry<\/a> designed by Swiss researchers could usher in a new era of gentle, automated robo-pickers.<\/p>\n The secret to picking a raspberry is to grip it just enough to get purchase and then pull it downwards off the little stem, apparently called the “receptacle,” which seems backwards. Seems simple \u2014 and it is, but only our hands are among the most sensitive and finely controlled constructions in the universe, the culmination of a hundred million years of evolution, outdone only by (I suspect) raccoons.<\/p>\n Robots simply don’t have the senses necessary to figure out the perfect technique for picking a berry. But what if it could communicate with the berry to better sense the forces involved and avoid either a a brutal crushing or humiliating failure-to-detach?<\/p> <\/div>\n That’s what Kai Junge, a PhD student at EPFL in Switzerland, aims to accomplish with this “sensorized raspberry,” a silicone and silicon replica berry that provides feedback to the picking machine, allowing it to learn to pick faster and better \u2014 and cleaner.<\/p>\n “It\u2019s an exciting dilemma for us as robotics engineers,” said professor Josie Hughes, who worked with Junge on the project. “The raspberry harvesting season is so short, and the fruit is so valuable, that wasting them simply isn’t an option. What’s more, the cost and logistical challenges of testing different options out in the field are prohibitive. That\u2019s why we decided to run our tests in the lab and develop a replica raspberry for training harvesting robots.”<\/p>\n Apparently the hard part comes just at the moment of detaching, when the force needed to grip the berry on the receptacle suddenly becomes overkill as the object goes from solid to hollow.<\/p>\n The replica berry has a fluidic sensor that tells the system how much compression is being experienced by the silicone drooplets, allowing the control model to learn how to adjust its grip as if the berry itself is telling it how much is too much.<\/p>\n You can see the berry in action below:<\/p>\n <\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n<p>The team plans to present their work at RobotSoft in April. And once the raspberry question is decided, they may move on to other berries, tomatoes, grapes&#8230; even apricots. The future is looking fresh!<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>If you&#8217;ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that&#8217;s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren&#8217;t super good at because they tend to be&#8230; crushy. -companies?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=8191"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292389,"date":"2022-03-31T11:55:17","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T18:55:17","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292389"},"modified":"2022-03-31T17:57:31","modified_gmt":"2022-04-01T00:57:31","slug":"all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination\/","title":{"rendered":"All eyes are on Swvl as it starts trading on a SPAC combination"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Mass transit and shared mobility provider <a href=\"https:\/\/www.swvl.com\/\">Swvl<\/a> went public today in <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. It\u2019s also a test for the company going public despite a market that\u2019s been unfriendly toward combinations with special purpose acquisition companies, or SPACs, of late.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Egypt-born and Dubai-based company has listed its shares at $10 on the Nasdaq through a merger with U.S. women-led blank check company Queen\u2019s Gambit Growth Capital. The planned merger, which will see Swvl offer 20-30% of its total shares, was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">announced last July<\/a>.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Following closing, the combined company, now \u201cSwvl Holding Corp,\u201d will trade under GMBT and GMBTW today before switching to SWVL and SWVLW on April 1.<\/span><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292389\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl is the first company launched from Africa and the second Middle Eastern company to list on the Nasdaq via a SPAC merger<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Anghami, an Abu Dhabi-based music streaming platform, <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">did so in February<\/a> when it listed with Vistas Media Acquisition at a $220 million valuation.<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/embed\/#?secret=CnJTROn2h9#?secret=Q5eMhyfACo\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl raised $121.5 million in private investment in public equities (PIPE) for this transaction<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. The European Bank for Reconstruction and Development (EBRD), Teklas Ventures, Chimera, Agility, and Luxor Capital Group are some of its other investors. The company is currently valued at $1.5 billion.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In February, one of its investors, Atalaya Capital, pulled out of the transaction. And in a filing, Queen\u2019s Gambit announced the termination of forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreements worth $100 million in SPAC shares and an extra $2 million via a private placement.<\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThe forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreement <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was done<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> with a group, and it was <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> access to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> capital,\u201d Queen\u2019s Gambit Capital founder and CEO Victoria Grace told TechCrunch when asked if the termination affects the deal.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cIts termination doesn\u2019t affect the valuation of the company or anything around our fundamental deal, which is Queen\u2019s Gambit merging with SWVL, so the valuation [stays] the same,\u201d she said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Investors withdrawing their interests and dollars from SPACs is not peculiar to Swvl. It\u2019s a usual occurrence &#8212; for instance, when BuzzFeed went public last December, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\">94% of the $287.5 million raised by the SPAC <\/a><\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was withdrawn<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> &#8212; particularly as the SPAC hype gives way in the face of an underperforming market and tighter regulation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Despite the seeming setback, there\u2019s good news for Swvl. <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to CFO Youssef Salem, the company has an <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional $600 million from proceeds and<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> committed equity facility with B. Riley Principal to access over the next few weeks if certain conditions are met, he said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Swvl was founded by <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">Mostafa Kandil<\/a>, Mahmoud Nouh and Ahmed Sabbah in 2017. The trio started the company as a bus-hailing service in Egypt and other ride-sharing services in emerging markets with fragmented public transportation.<\/p>\n<p>Its bus-hailing services enable users to make intra-state journeys by booking seats on buses running a fixed route. Swvl offerings have expanded beyond bus-hailing services, though. Now, the company offers inter-city rides, car ride-sharing, and corporate services in the 10 cities it operates in across Africa and the Middle East.<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The partnership between Swvl and Queen\u2019s Gambit came from a mutual interest from both parties<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While searching for a company to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">acquire<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl fit the blank-check company\u2019s criteria: strong business fundamentals, mobility and logistics (one of its core verticals), and an ESG ethos around women and affordable transportation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">On the other hand<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl &#8212; off the back of raising over $170 million in venture capital, expanding to over 16 countries across Latin America, Asia and Africa; hiring executives from Facebook, Uber and Optimus; and acquiring Shotl, Viapool and door2door &#8212; was on a quest for global dominance in the mobility space. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A SPAC with Queen\u2019s Gambit was the most suitable option for it from a financial standpoint, and both parties feel strongly about the sustainability angle around transport &#8212; Swvl claims it has prevented approximately 289 million pounds of carbon emissions since its inception.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The company plans to expand into several countries over the next six months, including Colombia, Mexico, South Africa, and the U.S. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In the meantime, all eyes will be on the company\u2019s performance as it <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">officially<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> starts trading tomorrow in a cooling SPAC market and a generally unsettled public market.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThere\u2019s a softness in the market, but as long as the company operates and delivers results, <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">maybe<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> today, people don\u2019t pay attention to it, but they will in months ahead,\u201d Grace said about the worrying SPAC and public markets.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201c<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I think<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> the market will change <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> like it always does and people go back to fundamentals at how we look at company\u2019s performances. For Swvl, they have been beating every single number that was ever presented to us. And that\u2019s what makes me super excited about this. And that\u2019s the type of target you want to partner with.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/\">Almost everything you need to know about SPACs<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Almost everything you need to know about SPACs&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/embed\/#?secret=dbGVg33T0n#?secret=s9kBhwdIHM\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Mass transit and shared mobility provider Swvl went public today in a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems. /tc_video?tags=21691"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576814951,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/corporate-services\/","name":"corporate services","slug":"corporate-services","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576814951"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576814951"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":52630,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/dubai\/","name":"Dubai","slug":"dubai","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/52630"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=52630"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292372,"date":"2022-03-31T12:05:44","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T19:05:44","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292372"},"modified":"2022-03-31T13:58:42","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T20:58:42","slug":"microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings\/","title":{"rendered":"Microsoft acquires process mining vendor Minit to grow its automation offerings"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Minit<\/a>, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which of those processes are ripe for automation.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Minit currently enables businesses to transform the way they analyze, monitor and optimize their processes. Minit\u2019s solutions have helped businesses gain deep insights into how processes run, uncover root causes of operational challenges and help mitigate undesired process outcomes,&#8221; Justin Graham, Microsoft&#8217;s general manager of process insights, wrote in a <a href=\"https:\/\/blogs.microsoft.com\/blog\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-minit-to-strengthen-process-mining-capabilities\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Microsoft&#8217;s corporate blog. &#8220;[With Minit, our] customers will be able to better understand their process data, uncover what operations look like in reality, and drive process standardization and improvement across the entire organization to ensure compliance at every step.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft dipped its toes into process mining with the launch of new features in Power Automate in 2019 and the acquisition of Softomotive, an RPA software provider, a year later. But with Minit, the tech giant is doubling down on a software category that could be worth over $11 billion by 2030, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wfmz.com\/news\/pr_newswire\/pr_newswire_technology\/global-process-mining-software-market-size-value-estimated-to-reach-usd-11-096-7-million\/article_a95b3354-ec2f-5389-b761-e4dbbdadbb97.html#:~:text=According%20to%20research%20report%20published,forecast%20period%202022%20to%202030.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according<\/a> to a report from Polaris Market Research.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292372\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>It wasn&#8217;t immediately clear whether the whole of the Minit team will join Microsoft &#8212; or, indeed, whether the company will remain spread across its current locations. (Minit is now headquartered in Amsterdam, with satellite offices in London and New York.) But CEO James Dening said that customers shouldn&#8217;t expect a change in the level of support they&#8217;re currently receiving.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We are looking forward to what it means to become part of an industry leader like Microsoft and what that brings us &#8212; how we can use that scale and excellence to continue to deliver great solutions to our customers,&#8221; Dening wrote in a blog <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/blog\/microsoft-minit-acquisition\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Minit&#8217;s website. &#8220;It has been a privilege to lead the company for the last year, and I\u2019m excited to continue my journey with the team, as part of what I consider to be the world\u2019s leading software company.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>In a statement, Microsoft spokesperson Zara Huang told TechCrunch that the Minit team will move into the\u00a0<span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> Process Insights team and that there will be &#8220;no change&#8221; to the current work location of Minit team members. <span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> is in early stages of determining how Minit will be integrated into its offerings, she said, and the companies will share more details when they&#8217;re available.<\/p>\n<p>Minit, which was founded in 2015 by Rasto Hlavac and had raised \u20ac10.3 million (~$11.40 million) prior to the acquisition, is one of an expanding number of startups developing process mining tools aimed at enterprise clientele. Process mining, also known as task discovery, involves spotting root cause workflow issues and bottlenecks by pulling data from systems including desktop, email apps and workflows. It&#8217;s a key part of robotic process automation (RPA), a technology that promises to automate monotonous, repetitive tasks traditionally performed by human workers while at the same time generating logs to identify potential cost savings.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>As Protocol&#8217;s Aisha Counts <a href=\"https:\/\/www.protocol.com\/bulletins\/microsoft-process-mining-minit\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">notes<\/a>, process mining has traditionally been done by system integrators who map out processes by analyzing manual workflows. Process mining software is designed to digitize the approach in a way that reduces the expense, time and effort involved.<\/p>\n<p>Underlining the appetite for process mining technologies, Celonis, a data processing company, earlier this week acquired Minit competitor Process Analytics Factory, which coincidentally integrates with Microsoft&#8217;s Power BI analytics platform. Just in the past several years, RPA vendor Automation Anywhere acquired process discovery and mining startups FortressIQ, Process Gold\\ and StepShot; Blue Prism released a task mining solution called Capture; and rivals including ABBYY and Kryon have expanded their process mining offerings.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/\">Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/embed\/#?secret=wqSRCOP7wQ#?secret=2NKiKfcj0k\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;You know the process space is hot when even Microsoft, with its vast resources, has to buy its way in. I\u2019m sure Microsoft is seeing the same trends that we saw, which drove the combination of FortressIQ and Automation Anywhere,&#8221; Pankaj Chowdhry, EVP of discovery at Automation Anywhere and formerly CEO of FortressIQ, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Customers are starved for process data to help them navigate their transformation journeys and any vendor that doesn&#8217;t have best-in-class process capabilities will find itself challenged to offer a compelling solution to their customers.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft&#8217;s Minit acquisition comes at a time when the broader business process automation industry, which remains <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/robotic-automation-is-back\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">flush with cash<\/a>, heads toward general consolidation. SAP acquired German process automation company Signavio in January 2021, just before ServiceNow got into the RPA segment with the buyout of India-based Intellibot.io. IBM <a href=\"https:\/\/newsroom.ibm.com\/2021-04-15-IBM-to-Acquire-myInvenio-to-help-Organizations-Use-AI-powered-Automation-to-Better-Streamline-Business-Processes\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">acquired<\/a> process mining software company MyInvenio in April. And Salesforce\u2019s MuleSoft and Microsoft followed suit with the purchases of automation tech providers <a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/08\/02\/mulesoft-acquires-rpa-provider-servicetrace\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Servicetrace<\/a>\u00a0and\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/10\/22\/microsoft-acquires-clear-software-to-strengthen-process-automation-offerings\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Clear Software<\/a>, respectively.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Process mining, discovery and task mining has seen a lot of transformation with many acquisitions in the last year. [It] now appears to be maturing as a market and becoming commoditized under major automation platforms,&#8221; Saikat Ray, Gartner senior research director, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Gartner sees an emergence of automation platform vendors offering process mining and task mining as embedded capabilities, along with RPA.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><em>Updated at 4:15 p.m. ET, March 31, with quotes from Microsoft and Automation Anywhere.<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired Minit, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which runch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=6"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292473,"date":"2022-03-31T14:10:50","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:50","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292473"},"modified":"2022-03-31T14:10:57","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:57","slug":"better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation\/","title":{"rendered":"Better learning through &#8216;complex dough-manipulation&#8217;"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/20\/robotics-roundup-12\/\">focused on pizza<\/a>. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly straightforward platform onto which ingredients are added.<\/p>\n<p>I say \u201cfairly\u201d here because there are still complications. There\u2019s really no such thing as easy when it comes to building robots that can execute variations on a task at a large scale. Here it\u2019s the dough that presents the problem. Turning a soft and malleable ball of dough into a pizza crust is one of those things humans have figured out how to do efficiently, but it still proves difficult for robot workers.<\/p>\n<p>A team of researchers at MIT, CMU and UC San Diego set out to create what they\u2019ve deemed \u201ccomplex dough-manipulation.\u201d The system is separated into a two-step process, in which the robot must first determine the task and then execute it using a tool like a rolling pin. The system, <a href=\"https:\/\/news.mit.edu\/2022\/robotic-deformable-object-0331\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">DiffSkill<\/a>, involves teaching robots complex tasks in simulations.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292473\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>MIT notes:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>A \u201cteacher\u201d algorithm solves each step the robot must take to complete the task. Then, it trains a \u201cstudent\u201d machine-learning model that learns abstract ideas about when and how to execute each skill it needs during the task, like using a rolling pin. With this knowledge, the system reasons about how to execute the skills to complete the entire task.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>The researchers say the system outperformed those trained in the more traditional reinforcement learning model. \u201cOur framework provides a novel way for robots to acquire new skills. These skills can then be chained to solve more complex tasks which are beyond the capability of previous robot systems,\u201d says CSAIL grad student, Yunzhu Li.<\/p>\n<p>This is robotics, so the whole pizza thing is really an initial problem for a system designed to tackle a lot more tasks. The company points to the emerging field of eldercare robotics as a possible use going forward.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been focused on pizza. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly and JetBlue Technology Ventures talk VC climate tech and ESG at TC Sessions: Climate 2022"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Investment in climate tech is heating up almost as fast as climate change itself. In 2021, <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/23\/climate-investment\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">climate tech startups received $40+ billion<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> across more than 600 deals. That\u2019s more than double the capital investment made in 2020.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">As <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.spglobal.com\/esg\/insights\/key-esg-trends-in-2022\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">S&amp;P Global recently reported<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, corporate sustainability efforts are under increasing scrutiny from investors, regulators and the public at large \u2014 placing corporations in the spotlight to actually behave differently. As a result, many corporate venture capital firms \u2014 particularly those with strong Environmental Social Governance (ESG) policies \u2014 are increasingly interested in startups focused on climate change tech.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Our existential climate crisis, the climate tech that could mitigate it and the VCs committed to funding it will intersect in two different presentations at <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-climate-2022\/?utm_medium=article&amp;utm_campaign=climate2022&amp;utm_content=sosvjetblue&amp;utm_source=techcrunch&amp;promo=article03&amp;display=\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">TC Sessions: Climate 2022<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> (presented by Extreme Tech Challenge) in Berkeley, California on June 14.\u00a0<\/span><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2290943\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">We\u2019re thrilled to announce that Amy Burr, president of JetBlue Technology Ventures (JTV), and Pae Wu, partner at SOSV and CTO at IndieBio, will helm two different panels addressing climate tech investment, corporate social responsibility (CSR) and ESG.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Burr leads JTV at a time when JetBlue has increased its measurable steps to reduce its effects on climate change and to achieve net zero carbon emissions by 2040. Among other efforts, and a first for JetBlue, the company now ties <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.esgtoday.com\/jetblue-ties-senior-bonuses-to-esg-goals-launches-2040-net-zero-target\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">ESG targets to bonuses<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> for its senior leaders.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">As president, Burr shapes the strategic venture investment direction of JetBlue and facilitates integration of successful startup programs into the airline\u2019s overall corporate innovation initiatives. A sample of JTV\u2019s portfolio companies include Joby (trading publicly), Lacuna, Turnkey (acquired) and Universal Hydrogen.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Prior to joining JTV, Burr \u2014 one of the original founders of Virgin America \u2014 served at VX in various executive roles and led the merger integration with Alaska Airlines.<\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">At both SOSV and IndieBio, Wu is responsible for portfolio management and technical oversight. She\u2019s focused on funding early-stage climate startups, along with tracking the trends and timing of hot, climate-specific industries. A sample of SOVO portfolio companies include Apix, New Age Meats, Perfect Day and Re-Nuble.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Prior to joining IndieBio, Wu served as the scientific director of Alpha, Telef\u00f3nica\u2019s Barcelona-based moonshot factory. Her earlier career includes stints as science director at the U.S. Office of Naval Research (Global) and as a technical consultant at the Defense Advanced Research Projects Agency (DARPA).\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Don\u2019t miss this opportunity to hear from JTV\u2019s Amy Burr and SOSV\u2019s Pae Wu. You\u2019ll gain a deeper understanding of how investors think when it comes to investing in climate tech, and you\u2019ll learn how to \u2014 and why you should \u2014 build ESG policies into your startup from day one.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-climate-2022\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">TC Sessions: Climate 2022<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> is all about the growing wave of startups, technologies, scientists and engineers dedicated to saving our planet and, of course, the investors who finance them. Join us in-person on June 14 at UC Berkeley&#8217;s Zellerbach Auditorium. <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-climate-2022\/?utm_medium=article&amp;utm_campaign=climate2022&amp;utm_content=sosvjetblue&amp;utm_source=techcrunch&amp;promo=article03&amp;display=\" Take a look at who\u2019s coming and what you&#8217;ll learn from them.<\/span><\/p>\n<h3><span class=\"schedule-item__title\">Evolving from Scientist to Founder<\/span><\/h3>\n<p><em>Brought to you by <span class=\"sponsors-label__sponsor-name\"><a href=\"https:\/\/www.mayfield.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Mayfield<\/a><\/span><\/em><\/p>\n<p><span class=\"schedule-item__description\">How do you go from PhD to startup founder and beyond? In this session, Mammoth Biosciences co-founder &amp; CTO Janice Chen and Endpoint Health co-founder &amp; CSO Diego Rey join Mayfield\u2019s Ursheet Parikh to share learnings from their own scientist-to-founder growth journeys. Learn how to go from bench to bedside and leverage scientific breakthroughs to save lives, how startups can ink productive partnerships with industry behemoths and more.<\/span><\/p>\n<h3><span class=\"schedule-item__title\">Financial stacks that scale from MVP to IPO<\/span><\/h3>\n<p><em>Brought to you by <span class=\"sponsors-label__sponsor-name\"><a href=\"https:\/\/brex.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Brex<\/a><\/span><\/em><\/p>\n<p><span class=\"schedule-item__description\">The best startup founders are visionaries &#8212; not operators. But the most successful startups are built to scale operationally from Day 1. In this panel discussion, Brex\u2019s directors of Product share their insights on the personal and practical choices early founders can make to streamline financial reporting and make their future CFOs proud. Even better? You can spend less time budgeting and more time building.<\/span><\/p>\n<h3><span class=\"schedule-item__title\">How to Talk Business When You\u2019re a Technical Founder<\/span><\/h3>\n<p><em>Brought to you by <span class=\"sponsors-label__sponsor-name\"><a href=\"https:\/\/www.dell.com\/en-us\/work\/shop\/techcrunch\/cp\/techcrunch\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dell for Startups<\/a><\/span><\/em><\/p>\n<p><span class=\"schedule-item__description\">When it comes to pitching early-stage enterprise startups, technical founders can sometimes neglect the business side of the conversation. To help build your confidence in \u201ctalking business,\u201d DTC\u2019s Ryan Wexler will cover the fundamentals of what investors want to hear about how you\u2019ll transform your technology into a fundamentally important business.<\/span><\/p>\n<h3><span class=\"schedule-item__title\">Top 10 Mistakes Early Founders Make<\/span><\/h3>\n<p><em>Brought to you by <span class=\"sponsors-label__sponsor-name\"><a href=\"http:\/\/aws.com\/startups\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Amazon Web Services<\/a><\/span><\/em><\/p>\n<p><span class=\"schedule-item__description\">What are the top mistakes early founders make while they are trying to reach product-market fit and how do you avoid them? In this presentation, Omar Valle will distill the lessons he has learned while working with over a thousand early-stage startups from top accelerators like Y Combinator, Techstars and StartX.<\/span><\/p>\n<h3><strong><span class=\"schedule-item__title\">Building a Web3 Platform Company<\/span><\/strong><\/h3>\n<p><em>Brought to you by <span class=\"sponsors-label__sponsor-name\"><a href=\"https:\/\/www.mayfield.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Mayfield<\/a><\/span><\/em><\/p>\n<p><span class=\"schedule-item__description\">How do you build a web3 platform company? Joe Lau, co-founder &amp; CTO of the world\u2019s leading blockchain developer platform Alchemy, joins Mayfield MD Navin Chaddha to share learnings from Alchemy\u2019s journey from inception to iconic. Join this session to learn about the inspiration behind Alchemy, how to find product-market fit in an emerging market, how to embed dev-centric into your DNA and more.<\/span><\/p>\n<h3><span class=\"schedule-item__title\">Setting the Foundation for Built-to-Last Companies<\/span><\/h3>\n<p><em>Brought to you by <span class=\"sponsors-label__sponsor-name\"><a href=\"https:\/\/www.mayfield.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Mayfield<\/a><\/span><\/em><\/p>\n<p><span class=\"schedule-item__description\">When it comes to company building, some things can\u2019t be retrofitted &#8212; they have to be set in place from day one. Join this session with Outreach co-founder &amp; CEO Manny Medina and Mayfield\u2019s Rajeev Batra as they share insights from Outreach\u2019s inception to iconic journey, including lessons learned on building an empathetic performance culture, embedding DEI into your DNA, the playbook for great category design and more.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-early-stage-2022\/?promo=partnersessionpostmar31\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">TechCrunch Early Stage<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u00a0takes place live and in-person on April 14. <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-early-stage-2022\/?promo=partnersessionpostmar31&amp;display=true\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Buy your pass now <\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">while you can save $200 and get ready for startup bootcamp. Yep, the<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/defi-the-future-of-programmable-money\/\"> DeFi &amp; The Future of Programmable Money<\/a> online event is that big. A truly global gathering of DeFi and crypto visionaries, builders and institutions working to create a new and improved future for finance.<\/p>\n<p>We want to call your attention to just some of the panel discussions and topics on tap tomorrow, but first \u2014 a quick public service announcement.<\/p>\n<p><b>Enter the no-token zone:<\/b> Attending DeFi &amp; The Future of Programmable Money is free, but<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/defi-the-future-of-programmable-money\/#tickets\"> you must register<\/a> to reserve your spot. The summit is in partnership with <a href=\"https:\/\/sommelier.finance\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sommelier Finance<\/a> \u2014 a leading crypto project created to automate decentralized finance trading \u2014 co-founded by Zaki Manian.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2286747\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>We now return to our regularly scheduled programming.<\/p>\n<p>DeFi can\u2019t happen without whip-smart engineers and data scientists, and you\u2019ll have the chance to hear from and engage with them tomorrow. Case in point \u2014 Volume\u2019s Taariq Lewis and Zhibai Zhang; Terra Incognita Capital\u2019s Erik Mayo and PeggyJV\u2019s Unique Divine. They\u2019ll hold forth in a presentation called:<\/p>\n<p><b>The rise of the DeFi quants and the new market wizards:<\/b> Data Scientist, Physicist, Engineer. The new market wizards of DeFi now wield the power of composable finance across the multichain. Hear how new software creates new financial markets.<\/p>\n<p>If you\u2019re curious about the state of structured products \u2014 and if you\u2019re not you should be \u2014 tune in to this session:<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><b>Decentralized Structured Products:<\/b> Structured Products, now coming to life in Decentralized Finance, lower the barriers for access to on-chain derivatives. What is the state of decentralized structured products and what\u2019s coming next?<\/p>\n<p>The presentation features Zaki Manian (Sommelier), Zubin Koticha (Opyn), Julian Koh (Ribbon Finance) and John Quinn (Decentral Park Capital). These folks may not have a crystal crypto ball, but they know their stuff. Engage in the conversation.<\/p>\n<p>DeFi may be heading toward the mainstream, but it will require quite a bit of heavy lifting to reach that destination. And that\u2019s why you won\u2019t want to miss this timely discussion:<\/p>\n<p><b>DeFi for the Masses:<\/b> It\u2019s still the early days of decentralized finance. What will the future bring and how can we build products fit for the masses? Join us for a conversation with founders working on bringing DeFi to the real world, a check-in on where we\u2019re going and how to get there.<\/p>\n<p>This panel\u2019s subject-matter experts include Patrick Baron (Moola Market), Rene Reinsberg (Celo Foundation), Jackie Bona (Valora) and Eric Cuellar (Node Wallet).<\/p>\n<p>There\u2019s plenty more to explore in the complete<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/defi-the-future-of-programmable-money\/#b933e0da-17e3-4191-9bfc-a64e635ead88\"> event agenda<\/a>. The<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/defi-the-future-of-programmable-money\/\"> DeFi &amp; The Future of Programmable Money<\/a> online summit kicks off this week on March 30.<\/p>\n<p>Decentralized finance is going mainstream, and we invite you to join the top crypto leaders, engineers, investors and regulators and come along for the ride. We\u2019re not kidding when we say this is your opportunity to hear from and engage with the biggest names in alternative finance.<\/p>\n<p><b>Pro Tip:<\/b> Attending DeFi &amp; The Future of Programmable Money is free, but<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/defi-the-future-of-programmable-money\/#tickets\"> you must register<\/a> to reserve your spot. The summit is in partnership with <a href=\"https:\/\/sommelier.finance\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sommelier Finance<\/a> \u2014 a leading crypto project created to automate decentralized finance trading \u2014 co-founded by Zaki Manian.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2286742\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Hold up, let\u2019s get back to those big names.<\/p>\n<p>It all starts with understanding <b>Why DeFi is the future of finance<\/b>. This panel features Zaki Manian (Sommelier), along with Adam Goldberg (Standard Crypo) and Sunny Aggarwal (Osmosis). These industry leaders will detail how DeFi differentiates from \u2014 and builds on \u2014 current centralized financial systems. Find out what\u2019s coming next and what it means for the future of finance.<\/p>\n<p>Enjoy even more interactive discussions with folks like Michael Egorov, the founder and CEO of Curve Financial \u2014 the King Kong of the crypto-verse. Don\u2019t miss <b>What is the state of DeFi today and why it is thriving<\/b>.<\/p>\n<p>You want more high-powered people? It\u2019s revolutionizing the way we move people, as well as parcels both big and small, and it\u2019s simultaneously reshaping the present and future of industries, cities and towns around the world.<\/p>\n<p>If you want to keep your fingers on mobility\u2019s driving pulse, you can\u2019t afford to miss <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-mobility-2022\/?utm_medium=tc_article_08&amp;utm_campaign=mobility2022&amp;utm_content=tc_article_08&amp;utm_source=techcrunch&amp;promo=tcarticle08&amp;display=\">TC Sessions: Mobility 2022<\/a>, a two-day, programming-packed summit covering all aspects of the mobility ecosystem. We\u2019re back live and in-person May 18-19 in San Mateo, California, with an online component on May 20.<\/p>\n<p>You also can\u2019t afford to miss our early-bird pricing \u2014 about which two things are true: It saves you a lot of cash, and it doesn\u2019t last forever. Your opportunity to save $300 is time-sensitive&#8230; and time is running out.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2282443\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-mobility-2022\/?utm_medium=tc_article_08&amp;utm_campaign=mobility2022&amp;utm_content=tc_article_08&amp;utm_source=techcrunch&amp;promo=tcarticle08&amp;display=true\">Buy your pass<\/a> by April 1 and keep three fat Franklins in your wallet \u2014 no foolin\u2019.<\/p>\n<p>What can you expect at <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-mobility-2022\/?utm_medium=tc_article_08&amp;utm_campaign=mobility2022&amp;utm_content=tc_article_08&amp;utm_source=techcrunch&amp;promo=tcarticle08&amp;display=\">TC Sessions: Mobility<\/a>? In a word, plenty. It starts with more than 2,000 attendees. You\u2019ll hear and learn from mobility\u2019s leading founders, CEOs, VCs and policymakers as TechCrunch editors ask tough, thought-provoking questions during one-on-one interviews and panel discussions.<\/p>\n<p>Case in point: <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/03\/learn-how-nuro-co-founder-jiajun-zhu-drove-the-av-startup-to-an-8-6b-valuation-at-tc-sessions-mobility-2022\/\">Jiajun Zhu<\/a>, co-founder and CEO of Nuro \u2014 the California-based AV behemoth that hit an $8.6 billion valuation last year \u2014 will be in the house for a 1:1 fireside chat. We can\u2019t wait to hear why Nuro steered clear of people and bet on delivering packages instead. We also want to learn more about the company\u2019s many high-profile partnerships, and that\u2019s just the tip of the conversation.<\/p>\n<p>Don\u2019t go skipping out on the smaller breakout sessions and topic-driven roundtable discussions. They\u2019re designed for taking conversations deeper and for making invaluable connections.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Karin Maake, senior director of communications at FlashParking, who attended our last in-person TC Mobility event (in 2019 thanks, pandemic), shared her experience with us.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI enjoyed the big marquee speakers from companies like Uber, but it was the individual presentations where you really started to get into the meat of the conversation and see how these mobile partnerships come to life.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>You\u2019ll find tons of prime networking opportunities everywhere, and especially in the huge indoor expo area where dozens of early-stage startups showcase and demo their products and tech. reality, rather than an alternative parallel financial system, can government regulators be far behind? In a word, no. But how do you regulate a system designed for remote, peer-to-peer and intermediary-free transactions \u2014 at an appropriate level \u2014 without stifling innovation?<\/p>\n<p>That\u2019s just one of many hot, and some might say controversial, topics you\u2019ll find at <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/defi-the-future-of-programmable-money\">DeFi &amp; The Future of Programmable Money<\/a>, a free, day-long virtual summit on March 30, 2022.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Pro Tip:<\/strong> Attending DeFi &amp; The Future of Programmable Money is free, but <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/defi-the-future-of-programmable-money\/#tickets\">you need to register<\/a> to secure your seat at the crypto table. The summit is sponsored by <a href=\"https:\/\/sommelier.finance\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sommelier Finance<\/a>, a leading crypto project, co-founded by Zaki Manian, designed to automate decentralized finance trading.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2281242\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>DeFi is a complex industry and regulating it is no small task. It\u2019s why we\u2019re excited to have Hester Peirce, who serves as SEC Commissioner, weigh in on this important topic and share her extensive knowledge and expertise.<\/p>\n<p>Peirce will be joined by Kristin Smith (The Blockchain Association), Miller Whitehouse-Levine (DeFi Education Fund) and Zaki Manian (Sommelier Finance) for a session called:<\/p>\n<p><strong>DeFi and Regulations:<\/strong> Regulation of DeFi is here (ish). How can regulators engage with the ecosystem productively and what can DeFi projects do to help bring regulators to the table?<\/p>\n<p>Peirce, who began serving as SEC Commissioner in January 2018, has a long and outspoken history of supporting the crypto industry, to the point where many in the community refer to her as \u201cCrypto Mom.\u201d We can\u2019t wait to hear her thoughts on what it might take to create a realistic regulatory framework.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Regulators are coming for crypto. Bring your questions and engage in what\u2019s sure to be a lively conversation. Connect with influential movers and shippers at TC Sessions: Mobility 2022"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">If you\u2019re itching to get your game-changing product out of the garage, onto the streets or into customers\u2019 driveways, we not-so-humbly suggest that you do whatever it takes to attend <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-mobility-2022\/?utm_medium=tc_article_03&amp;utm_campaign=mobility2022&amp;utm_content=tc_article_03&amp;utm_source=techcrunch&amp;promo=tcarticle03&amp;display=\">TC Sessions: Mobility 2022<\/a> in San Mateo, California on May 18-19. It\u2019s your chance to meet, mingle and network with mobility\u2019s movers, shakers, shippers and unicorn makers under one roof at the spacious San Mateo County Event Center.<\/p>\n<p>Who\u2019s at the top of your must-meet list? Whether it\u2019s top VCs, cutting-edge mobility companies, government policy makers, visionary engineers or tech journalists \u2014 to score coveted media exposure \u2014 you\u2019ll find that and more waiting for you in two action-packed days at TC Mobility.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Hot tip No. 1:<\/strong> Early-bird savings are in play \u2014 for a limited time. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-mobility-2022\/?utm_medium=tc_article_03&amp;utm_campaign=mobility2022&amp;utm_content=tc_article_03&amp;utm_source=techcrunch&amp;promo=tcarticle03&amp;display=true\">Buy your pass now<\/a>, before prices increase, and you\u2019ll keep $300 in your wallet. Sweet, sweet savings.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2275698\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Your all-access pass includes panel discussions, 1:1 interviews, breakout sessions and networking, plus access to our indoor AND outdoor expo area \u2014 where you\u2019ll find dozens of innovative early-stage startups demoing their latest and greatest. More on that in a moment. You\u2019ll also have access to our day of online content on May 20. Oh, plus videos on-demand following the live event.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Hot tip No. 2:<\/strong> If you want to place your mobility tech directly in the path of thousands of attendees \u2014 we\u2019re talking potential investors, customers and influential tech titans \u2014 <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-mobility-2022\/?utm_medium=tc_article_03&amp;utm_campaign=mobility2022&amp;utm_content=tc_article_03&amp;utm_source=techcrunch&amp;promo=tcarticle03&amp;display=true\">grab an Early-Stage Startup Demo Package<\/a>. Don\u2019t wait. The early-bird special saves you $200. You&#8217;ll get four passes with full access to the event, both in-person and virtually, the ability to demo on-site on May 18 and 19, and the ability to pitch during the online event on May 20.<\/p>\n<p>Okay, let\u2019s go back to the expo area. The huge indoor space expands into the great outdoors. You\u2019ll find demos spanning the range of mobility tech, including the latest in scooters, e-bikes, EVs and autonomous vehicles. Test drive to your heart\u2019s content or snag a Startup Demo Package and showcase your mobile marvel in our outdoor playground.<\/p>\n<p>Take it from Jens Lehmann, technical lead and product manager, SAP, who had this to say about our last in-person mobility event back in 2019 (thanks a bunch, pandemic): \u201cThe most surprising aspect of TC Sessions: Mobility was just how much fun I had while learning. I can\u2019t emphasize that enough. I got to drive the latest and greatest electric scooters, and I rode around in a VR\/AR-enhanced car. tech steps into the spotlight at TC Sessions: Climate 2022"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">It\u2019s going to take a whole lot more than electric cars and plant-based foods to change the course of climate change, the most critical, existential crisis in human history. Climate tech isn\u2019t just one industry: it\u2019s every industry in every country across the globe. And it\u2019s why we\u2019re launching our first climate tech summit \u2014 <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/tc-sessions-climate-2022\/?utm_medium=article&amp;utm_campaign=climate2022&amp;utm_content=eventannouncement&amp;utm_source=techcrunch&amp;promo=article01&amp;display=\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">TC Sessions: Climate 2022<\/a> \u2014 live at UC Berkley&#8217;s Zellerbach Auditorium in Berkeley, California, on June 14, with a virtual event to follow on June 16.<\/p>\n<p>Join more than 1,000 people dedicated to saving our planet and its inhabitants. Hear from and engage with in-the-know early-stage founders and CEOs with serious science and engineering bonafides. And there\u2019s more \u2014 double the venue space, twice as much content and, at more than 2,000, twice as many attendees. about LobsterDAO, an influential community of engineers, devs and founders at DeFi &#038; The Future of Programmable Money"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/defi-the-future-of-programmable-money\/?utm_medium=tc_article_01&amp;utm_campaign=defisummit&amp;utm_content=tc_article_01&amp;utm_source=techcrunch&amp;promo=tc_article01&amp;display=true\">DeFi &amp; The Future of Programmable Money<\/a>, a one-day virtual conference on March 30, offers something for everyone involved with, or interested in learning about, the bleeding-edge world of decentralized finance. While there\u2019s plenty of talk about crypto whales, a different sea creature is making waves \u2014 and a community \u2014 for current or aspiring DeFi engineers and developers.<\/p>\n<p>More on that in a moment, but first a bit of necessary housekeeping.<\/p>\n<p><b>Gas Capped:<\/b> Attending DeFi &amp;The Future of Programmable Money is free, but you must <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/defi-the-future-of-programmable-money\/?utm_medium=tc_article_01&amp;utm_campaign=defisummit&amp;utm_content=tc_article_01&amp;utm_source=techcrunch&amp;promo=tc_article01&amp;display=true\">register here<\/a> to reserve your seat. The summit is in partnership with <a href=\"https:\/\/sommelier.finance\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sommelier Finance<\/a>, a leading crypto project, co-founded by Zaki Manian, and designed to automate decentralized finance trading.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2272113\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Okay, let\u2019s get back to that other sea beast we mentioned earlier. It\u2019s a 17,950-strong (and growing) community known collectively as LobsterDAO (see what we did there?). One of the most active and engaged DeFi communities, it\u2019s a resource where engineers, developers, founders and builders can discuss, among other things, open source DeFi and programmable money code.<\/p>\n<p>The group describes<a href=\"https:\/\/t.me\/blockchain_lobsters\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> its purpose<\/a> as \u201cfirst and foremost a crypto community for technical and economic research and discussion, with a strong focus on DeFi.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>LobsterDAO began as an open research chat on Telegram\u2019s instant messaging platform in 2018. The space, which remains free from marketing or paid promotions, provides an environment where engineers, developers and founders can discuss their own projects and technology, debate hacks and talk about other web3 topics, projects and apps.<\/p>\n<p>While the DeFi community, in general, stretches the etiquette boundaries associated with traditional finance, LobsterDAO\u2019s crustacean community pushes them hard. Case in point, one of the community\u2019s many sub-channels, Blockchain Lobsters (with 7,734 subscribers), self-describes as \u201cA collection of drunk opinions and stats on crypto and startups.\u201d<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Things can get pretty salty down under the sea.<\/p>\n<p>Don\u2019t be misled by this free-wheeling attitude. You\u2019ll likely find that active members of the LobsterDAO community include influential DeFi heavyweights and creators of major crypto protocols.<\/p>\n<p>LobsterDAO gave birth to Curve Finance, and other projects that have collaborated with this community include GearBox, Ambire, CoinList, Icy.tools and DexGuru.<\/p>\n<p>In addition to the main channel, and the aforementioned Blockchain Lobsters, other sub-channels include a main DeFi chat, a DeFi dev chat, a daily newsletter, a job board and two NFT-related chats \u2014 NFT Avenue and Seafood Kingdom.<\/p>\n<p>You\u2019ll have the opportunity to learn even more about LobsterDAO at the DeFi &amp;The Future of Programmable Money summit. That\u2019s where you\u2019ll find Ivangbi, builder of narratives at LobsterDAO and Gearbox.<\/p>\n<p>He, along with Michael Egorov (Curve Finance), Vasiliy Shapovalov (LIDO) and Taariq Lewis (Volume) will conduct a session called <b>What is the state of DeFi today and why is it thriving?<\/b> Bring your questions, get ready for an engaging, informative, experience and be sure to<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/defi-the-future-of-programmable-money\/#b933e0da-17e3-4191-9bfc-a64e635ead88\"> check the day\u2019s agenda<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>DeFi &amp; The Future of Programmable Money is free and takes place on March 30.<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/events\/defi-the-future-of-programmable-money\/?utm_medium=tc_article_01&amp;utm_campaign=defisummit&amp;utm_content=tc_article_01&amp;utm_source=techcrunch&amp;promo=tc_article01&amp;display=true\"> Register here<\/a> to reserve your seat, and explore this aquatic community where engineers, devs, builders and founders make waves \u2014 and change \u2014 in the world of DeFi.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>DeFi &amp; The Future of Programmable Money, a one-day virtual conference on March 30, offers something for everyone involved with, or interested in learning about, the bleeding-edge world of decentralized finance.
